  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d6c2cccf-074e-42c0-a11e-f33f69e62d39'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText18344325142313587261" style="display:none">Evacuated from Blitz-battered London, shy and genteel Elizabeth White is sent to stay with the boisterous O'Connors in Kilgarret, Ireland. It is the beginning of an unshakeable bond between Elizabeth and Aisling O'Connor, a friendship which will endure through twenty turbulent years of change and chaos, joy and sorrow, soaring dreams and searing betrayals...<br /><br />Writing with warmth, wit and great compassion, Maeve Binchy tells a magnificent story of the lives and loves of two women, bound together in a friendship that nothing could tear asunder - not even the man who threatened to come between them forever.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2320941542" />
    <a title="Loretta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18967405-loretta"><img alt="Loretta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605997826p2/18967405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320941542?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Loretta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Loretta" href="/user/show/18967405-loretta">Loretta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18967405-loretta?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18967405-loretta?shelf=my-2018-reading-challenge">my-2018-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320941542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14049708925675229375">While I did enjoy Binchy's writing and her beautiful character development, the beginning of the book was far more enjoyable than the latter part which did just seem to drag on and on. I feel that this book would have served the reader a better experience with more enjoyment had it been broken down into a trilogy. More a 3.5 than a 4 but I always round up my star ratings. 😊 </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_7082485" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7082485" />
    <a title="Sue Evans" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/440239-sue-evans"><img alt="Sue Evans" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440531869p2/440239.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7082485?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue Evans" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue Evans" href="/user/show/440239-sue-evans">Sue Evans</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7082485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2460486796527842873">This was my first Binchy and I absolutely loved it until the last couple of chapters.<br/>I felt perhaps since this was Binchy's first published book, maybe she struggled with how to end it. The main characters seemed to be "out of character" in the last few chapters and a lot of the way it ended didn't fit with the rest of the story.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8693677058919581710">Oh, how I miss Maeve! She was such a special writer. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1583052158i/29040444.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was her first novel. I must have read it back in the 1980s. Luckily, I barely remembered a thing. I don’t enjoy re-reading fiction when I remember stuff. I made that mistake with Isabel Allende’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/909224509?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>The House of the Spirits</a>.   <span id="freeText8693677058919581710" style="display:none">Oh, how I miss Maeve! She was such a special writer. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1583052158i/29040444.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was her first novel. I must have read it back in the 1980s. Luckily, I barely remembered a thing. I don’t enjoy re-reading fiction when I remember stuff. I made that mistake with Isabel Allende’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/909224509?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The House of the Spirits</a>. Loved it the first time. Decided to re-read it a few years later when not enough time had passed. The magic was gone. I enjoyed this book as much as I did the first time that I read it. <br><br>This is a story of a friendship between two girls, set in Ireland and England in the 1940s and 1950s. The characters were complex and well-developed, as they always are with Maeve. The story grabbed me, and I was thinking about it constantly any time that I wasn’t reading – always a good sign! <br><br>The only reason that I am not giving it 5 stars is the ending. It was fabulous all the way through, but the ending just seemed rushed, flat, out of character, and a bit bizarre. It threw me for a loop, and I had to check if I was missing anything. This book is worth reading for all the lovely parts, but just be aware that the ending is weak. <br><br>My favorite quote: <br><br>“Self-pity brings tears to the eyes quicker than anything else.”</span>

<div id="review_51950431" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51950431" />
    <a title="Meghan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695170-meghan"><img alt="Meghan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499028194p2/695170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51950431?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meghan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meghan" href="/user/show/695170-meghan">Meghan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451203045" href="/book/show/771525.Light_a_Penny_Candle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51950431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13752350204580065919">I find it hard to objectively review or even rate any of Maeve Binchy's books. I don't pick up any of her novels with the intent of exploring some deep philosophical or cultural questions. Instead, I approach each of her novels as an imaginary journey, a very long movie that plays out through words. The characters she creates in all of her novels are both realistic and engaging and Light a Penny Candle is no exception. Once again, I found myself breezing through the pages, so desperate to find o</span>
  <span id="freeText13752350204580065919" style="display:none">I find it hard to objectively review or even rate any of Maeve Binchy's books. I don't pick up any of her novels with the intent of exploring some deep philosophical or cultural questions. Instead, I approach each of her novels as an imaginary journey, a very long movie that plays out through words. The characters she creates in all of her novels are both realistic and engaging and Light a Penny Candle is no exception. Once again, I found myself breezing through the pages, so desperate to find out what happened next to Elizabeth, Aisling and the rest (yes, even Johnny Stone...) only to find myself equally as reluctant to turn that last page and see their stories end. But that's the thing, their stories don't really end. It felt almost as if Binchy had recognized that she needed to end the novel at some point or else she could have gone on forever, following all of the remaining characters throughout the rest of their lives. And I think it is this impulse, the idea that I truly can imagine a whole new set of encounters and exchanges between these characters, that draws me to Binchy as an author. No, Light a Penny Candle does not provide much in the way of heavy discussion, but as far as pure entertainment, I think Binchy is miles ahead of most others. My rating (5 out of 5) may be biased, and possibly influenced by her recent passing, but I think this novel holds its own in her collection against some of my favorites (Circle of Friends, Echoes and Tara Road). If you're looking for some quality escapist literature, I highly recommend this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13752350204580065919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_362751451" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/362751451" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7374796-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541332951p2/7374796.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/362751451?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/7374796-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362751451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15704262254968640327">I know all kinds of women who read Maeve Binchy. Friends and relatives all like her.<br/><br/>Why?<br/><br/>I think its partly because she writes so well about the Irish. She has a knack for showing what Irish Catholics do, believe in, think about etc. <br/><br/>“Light a Penny Candle” begins in the 1940's and ends in 1959. It tells of a very different era from our own. Now we counsel women to leave their alcoholic and violent husbands; then, Irish Catholic mothers told their daughters that it was their duty to stay with such</span>
  <span id="freeText15704262254968640327" style="display:none">I know all kinds of women who read Maeve Binchy. Friends and relatives all like her.<br /><br />Why?<br /><br />I think its partly because she writes so well about the Irish. She has a knack for showing what Irish Catholics do, believe in, think about etc. <br /><br />“Light a Penny Candle” begins in the 1940's and ends in 1959. It tells of a very different era from our own. Now we counsel women to leave their alcoholic and violent husbands; then, Irish Catholic mothers told their daughters that it was their duty to stay with such men because of the sanctity of marriage! <br /><br />I read this novel pretty quickly and so did my mother, who started it and left all her other books behind to focus on it. The pacing is good, though the beginning and end are a bit slow.<br /><br />My main criticism of the novel is its ending. I won’t spoil it by revealing too much, but I feel that certain characters changed unexpectedly and unbelievably. Binchy didn’t prepare her reader for an ending that seemed rushed or contrived.<br /><br />Is “Light a Penny Candle” fluffy romance for women? <br /><br />I don’t think so. The novel tells us so a lot about Irish customs and ways, and it gives us a glimpse of England during WW2 .<br /><br />I’ll have to read more of her to see what her (many) later novels become. She’s written lots and lots of books, which makes me wonder if she slides into more formulaic writing.<br /><br />I’ll have to see! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15704262254968640327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_614014368" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/614014368" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2825213-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483412885p2/2825213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/614014368?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/2825213-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2825213-kathryn?shelf=reading-list-2014">reading-list-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2825213-kathryn?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2825213-kathryn?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer614014368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16697604991954651733">Wow. This was…not what I expected from Maeve Binchy’s debut novel. I have read and enjoyed many Maeve Binchy’s works before this (I just counted - looks like I’ve read 15!), and I enjoyed most of this one, but was slightly disappointed by the ending. It felt like a rather more dark work than I was anticipating. <br/><br/>It was quite long - over 800 pages - but an easy read, chronicling the lives of 2 young girls as they grow up together during the war, turn into young women on opposite sides of the Irish</span>
  <span id="freeText16697604991954651733" style="display:none">Wow. This was…not what I expected from Maeve Binchy’s debut novel. I have read and enjoyed many Maeve Binchy’s works before this (I just counted - looks like I’ve read 15!), and I enjoyed most of this one, but was slightly disappointed by the ending. It felt like a rather more dark work than I was anticipating. <br /><br />It was quite long - over 800 pages - but an easy read, chronicling the lives of 2 young girls as they grow up together during the war, turn into young women on opposite sides of the Irish Sea, while continuing their friendship, knowing that they can always count on the other, if needed.<br /><br />I loved the story, parts of which were heartbreaking, and while I can see how the ending could have happened, I didn’t like it (and I can’t explain why, without giving everything away) and I didn’t like the writing style about 30 pages from the end. It became choppy, and was obviously intentional, in 2 - 3 sentence bursts of action at a time, before moving the spotlight on to the next character’s piece of action.<br /><br />I was tempted to drop my rating, but left it at 4 stars, because even though I didn’t like the ending, I suppose it was well done, and my dislike is purely personal bias.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16697604991954651733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2315884635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11521434517753811854">This book is long! 824 pages. I bought it, second- hand, in paperback and it was so thick that (having become used to reading on a Kindle) it felt quite uncomfortable to hold at first. <br/>I’m an avid reader of crime fiction, and when the story opened with a ‘flash-forward’ in a coroner’s court, I found myself expecting a murder to occur. Eventually, I realised that it wasn’t that kind of story and I became immersed in the engaging saga of two women’s friendship. <br/>Vivid characterisation really is the</span>
  <span id="freeText11521434517753811854" style="display:none">This book is long! 824 pages. I bought it, second- hand, in paperback and it was so thick that (having become used to reading on a Kindle) it felt quite uncomfortable to hold at first. <br />I’m an avid reader of crime fiction, and when the story opened with a ‘flash-forward’ in a coroner’s court, I found myself expecting a murder to occur. Eventually, I realised that it wasn’t that kind of story and I became immersed in the engaging saga of two women’s friendship. <br />Vivid characterisation really is the heart of this book. The main characters are loveable, especially lively red-head Aisling. There was a large supporting cast of distinctive characters: fun-loving Harry, narcissistic Johnny, moaning Maureen. I felt that I was supposed to like Eileen but I found her prematurely old demeanour and judgemental Catholicism quite unattractive. I couldn’t really relate to Simon and Henry – at first I assumed they were a gay couple – how wrong I was! <br />And then, after 814 pages <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ a murder does occur. It was what I’d expected in the beginning and had given up on, and when it came I found it the least believable and most unsatisfying part of the book.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I’d been suckered.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11521434517753811854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_396334006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Nicholas During" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/440220-nicholas-during"><img alt="Nicholas During" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306953644p2/440220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/396334006?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicholas During" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicholas During" href="/user/show/440220-nicholas-during">Nicholas During</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451222640" href="/book/show/443470.Light_a_Penny_Candle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer396334006&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer396334006" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3417304871165799177">I was pretty disappointed in this book overall. It starts off well, and I was at first enjoying it a lot. But though the writing has energy and drive, the themes never are really given their due, the characters are introduced and barely slip out of a form character for the rest of the novel (which is meant to be 20 years of their lives), there isn't really any consequences to their actions, and I felt like the whole things was a bit shallow. <br/><br/>But rather than being totally negative I'll note the t</span>
  <span id="freeText3417304871165799177" style="display:none">I was pretty disappointed in this book overall. It starts off well, and I was at first enjoying it a lot. But though the writing has energy and drive, the themes never are really given their due, the characters are introduced and barely slip out of a form character for the rest of the novel (which is meant to be 20 years of their lives), there isn't really any consequences to their actions, and I felt like the whole things was a bit shallow. <br /><br />But rather than being totally negative I'll note the two things I did like: Elizabeth White as a child was stronger. Mostly because we were able to see her adapt to a new country, family, and culture and see her change there—which doesn't happen at all in the rest of the novel, and when Eileen changes her mind about her daughter's separation from her husband it doesn't seem anyone cares anyway. And the relationship between the strong independent woman when Aisling moves to London. Though I totally saw Aisling and Johnny's relationship coming, I did like that she has Aisling ending the book as single, childless, but content and willing to duke it out in the tough streets on London rather than returning to her familial Irish tough. <br /><br />But otherwise the book fell flat for me. And in particular the male characters. Only the Irish men has something there. Johnny, meant to be so seductive, is just boring and juvenile. Didn't do it for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3417304871165799177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Annie Kaye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7143753-annie-kaye"><img alt="Annie Kaye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458091181p2/7143753.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer543585545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7444467496390428397">3.5 stars.<br/><br/>I won't go into the details of the book itself - other reviewers have done so. This is the first Maeve Binchy book I've read where I finished it and felt rather unsatisfied. I have become accustomed to (and a fan of) the way she spins a tale, weaves together the details, and above all exercises the patience to do the story justice. <br/><br/>However, the wheels seemed to come off the story, so to speak, in the middle of the final chapter. It felt like she got tired of writing it and wasn't sure </span>
  <span id="freeText7444467496390428397" style="display:none">3.5 stars.<br /><br />I won't go into the details of the book itself - other reviewers have done so. This is the first Maeve Binchy book I've read where I finished it and felt rather unsatisfied. I have become accustomed to (and a fan of) the way she spins a tale, weaves together the details, and above all exercises the patience to do the story justice. <br /><br />However, the wheels seemed to come off the story, so to speak, in the middle of the final chapter. It felt like she got tired of writing it and wasn't sure how to wrap it up. The accelerated pace of the latter half of Chapter 16 was bumpy and out of step from the rest of the book. The ending was disorienting and abrupt. I didn't think it was the end, to be honest - listening to the audiobook, I thought the audio file was corrupted. <br /><br />I still recommend the story itself - I loved the friendship between Aisling and Elizabeth, and the love of Aisling's mother Eileen. Just be aware that you may find the ending less than satisfying. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7444467496390428397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer47653089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8653770002089631840">Maeve Binchy gives us characters who live, laugh, and love. I always think she will give me something light to read because her writing is effortless and, frankly, she doesn't exactly challenge one's thinking. But there is also always something extra to learn, perhaps something to add to one's own way of dealing with life. Light a Penny Candle is a delight.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100201187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6605334442566399770">I read this book in the Christmas break of 1983 and loved the warmth that flowed from the page. IN 1994 I saw Maeve speak here in Melbourne and her warmth and interest in her fellow human is as alive and real as her characters. She believes we each have a story that we should write. Her stories of her mother and father were truly hilarious. She usually publishes a novel every two years and I have them all. I reread them when I just feel the need to retreat away with something lovely.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51143077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8518001183261476030">It's 1940s & Hitler is planning his war on England. To protect their 10 year old daughter Elizabeth, George White and his wife send her to Kilgarret, Ireland. Taken in by her mother's old school friend, Eileen O'Connor, & her husband Sean, Elizabeth quickly becomes inseparable from their vivacious daughter Aisling.   <span id="freeText8518001183261476030" style="display:none">It's 1940s &amp; Hitler is planning his war on England. To protect their 10 year old daughter Elizabeth, George White and his wife send her to Kilgarret, Ireland. Taken in by her mother's old school friend, Eileen O'Connor, &amp; her husband Sean, Elizabeth quickly becomes inseparable from their vivacious daughter Aisling. It is Aisling who teaches Elizabeth to have faith in life and convinces her that if you light a penny candle at church, your most sacred wish will come true. Five years later, Elizabeth returns home armed with a new sense of independence and love of life. Against her parents' wishes, she pursues a career in art and embarks on a no-strings-attached love affair that threatens to break her heart. Meanwhile, Aisling remains in Kilgarret, yearning for a larger world, a world more like Elizabeth's. Passionately courted by the son of Kilgarret's wealthiest families, she struggles to convince herself tht he could make her happy. From the moment they meet to the moment two decades later when they know they both love the same elusive, irrestible man, their lives are inextricably linked. Two women caought between the past and the future, theirs is a world swept up in change...a world where old ways no longer work and new ways demand daring...a world where in times of trouble, it is no longer enough to Light a Penny Candle.<br /></span>

        <a title="Rowena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rowena" href="/user/show/179200-rowena">Rowena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32911930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9480192555777519841">This is the story of Elizabeth White and Aisling O'Connor. Elizabeth is sent to stay with Aisling's family in Ireland during the Blitz in London. The two of them grow to be best friends despite of, or perhaps because of the events that occur over the next two decades. <br/><br/>I can't really explain why I enjoy Maeve Binchy's books so much. The writing isn't particularly profound and her plots tend to veer toward extreme soap opera-iness. However, each and every one of her characters are so well-develope</span>
  <span id="freeText9480192555777519841" style="display:none">This is the story of Elizabeth White and Aisling O'Connor. Elizabeth is sent to stay with Aisling's family in Ireland during the Blitz in London. The two of them grow to be best friends despite of, or perhaps because of the events that occur over the next two decades. <br /><br />I can't really explain why I enjoy Maeve Binchy's books so much. The writing isn't particularly profound and her plots tend to veer toward extreme soap opera-iness. However, each and every one of her characters are so well-developed and so HUMAN that I can't help but be drawn to each of them. Furthermore, MB has the knack of richly portraying Ireland and her people...their speech, mannerisms, customs, humor, pathos...everything. For me, it's a real treat to read one of MB's novels because it takes me somewhere so unspeakably foreign yet, as so many reviewers have touted, makes me feel like I've come home. Cheesy, but true.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9480192555777519841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_586250613" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/586250613" />
    <a title="Megan Odonoghue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16096998-megan-odonoghue"><img alt="Megan Odonoghue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357794170p2/16096998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/586250613?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan Odonoghue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan Odonoghue" href="/user/show/16096998-megan-odonoghue">Megan Odonoghue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer586250613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9987124523510659264">Evacuated from Blitz-battered London, shy and genteel Elizabeth White is sent to stay with the boisterous O’Connors in Kilgarret, Ireland. It is the beginning of an unshakeable bond between Elizabeth and Aisling O’Connor, a friendship that will endure through twenty turbulent years of change and chaos, joy and sorrow, soaring dreams and searing betrayals. Through those years of friendship Aisling and Elizabeth wind in and out of each other’s lives. As they grow, fall in love, through happy times</span>
  <span id="freeText9987124523510659264" style="display:none">Evacuated from Blitz-battered London, shy and genteel Elizabeth White is sent to stay with the boisterous O’Connors in Kilgarret, Ireland. It is the beginning of an unshakeable bond between Elizabeth and Aisling O’Connor, a friendship that will endure through twenty turbulent years of change and chaos, joy and sorrow, soaring dreams and searing betrayals. Through those years of friendship Aisling and Elizabeth wind in and out of each other’s lives. As they grow, fall in love, through happy times and disappointments, they come to realize that not all troubles will be solved, nor all wishes granted by lighting a penny candle.<br /><br />I first read Light a Penny Candle years ago when I was a teenager, it was the first Maeve Binchy book I read and by far my favorite, and through the years I have re-read it several times. I have read all of Binchy’s books, most are what I would call “easy reads” – light hearted and warm but a bit predictable. However when I recently read Light a Penny Candle again and remembered why I loved it so much and I still find myself completely immerse in the story.<br /><br />The characters are well written and strong; the story is one of friendship and the growth, struggle and joys that happen along the way. Maeve Binchy paints a glorious story of the lives and loves of two women bound together by friendship. I felt as though I was right alongside Aisling and Elizabeth in Ireland watching them grow into adulthood and confront family conflicts, love affairs, and failed marriages. <br /><br />The story evolves over 1940s to 1960s, and illuminates the stifling lack of privacy typical of small-town life.<br /><br />The only thing I disliked was the abrupt ending – it left me thirsting for more (a sign of a good book if you ask me), I wanted to know what happened to Aisling and Elizabeth after the book ended.<br /><br />Over the years, each time I would reached for a new Maeve Binchy book I found myself thinking of the girls of “Light a Penny Candle” where were they nao and how were they doing. I still have my original book (I got it from a church book swap) – it is old, tattered, and worn, but opening up its pages brings me home to a place I feel happy and comfortable, home to Kilgarret!<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://mjcod.wordpress.com/">http://mjcod.wordpress.com/</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9987124523510659264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/225897571?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/6147238-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer225897571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5171074091021697369">The first time I read a Bnchy novel, I was like, “Is this her best novel yet?” Oh, right. This is just one out of many. Reading another of her novel has not ruined my expectations of finding her words as moving and her characters as lively and real as those in the first I’ve read.<br/><br/>Really, it’s like, the people in the novel are not mere icons of fiction but they actually seem like you’re personally hearing their conversations. Every word the characters say is breaking my heart for the innate geniu</span>
  <span id="freeText5171074091021697369" style="display:none">The first time I read a Bnchy novel, I was like, “Is this her best novel yet?” Oh, right. This is just one out of many. Reading another of her novel has not ruined my expectations of finding her words as moving and her characters as lively and real as those in the first I’ve read.<br /><br />Really, it’s like, the people in the novel are not mere icons of fiction but they actually seem like you’re personally hearing their conversations. Every word the characters say is breaking my heart for the innate geniuses they have in them. It’s nice to see that these people are really trying to make something worthy out of their lives and Binchy never failed to make each of her characters have that overwhelming sense of strong and motivated personalities. <br /><br />Another thing why I love the novel so much is because of the tranquil environment amidst the bustling to-and-fro of mobs in a big city. You can still see a sense of peace although war is evidently going on. It’s like, when everything goes wrong, you still have a home to go to. The novel even proves more than just that.<br /><br />Generally, the novel is one masterpiece any genteel traveler would love to carry along whilst in a pleasant holiday trip. <br /><br />And oh, I like Johnny Stone so much. I was really hoping he'd change and be a gentleman and marry someone though. </span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Elmvang" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Elmvang" href="/user/show/168347-maria-elmvang">Maria Elmvang</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099196518" href="/book/show/1094776.Light_A_Penny_Candle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/168347-maria-elmvang?shelf=owned-physical-book">owned-physical-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/168347-maria-elmvang?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/168347-maria-elmvang?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2680354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8471955373785516931">Maeve Binchy's debut novel, and unfortunately it really shows. She hasn't found her own voice at all, and I kept thinking I was reading a Rosamunde Pilcher novel instead. Not that there's anything wrong with RP, I just missed the charm of Maeve Binchy's later books.<br/><br/>The thing I love about Maeve Binchy's books is that they're generally speaking comfort reads. There are exceptions of course, but as a rule people tend to be in a better place at the end of the book than they were at the beginning. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText8471955373785516931" style="display:none">Maeve Binchy's debut novel, and unfortunately it really shows. She hasn't found her own voice at all, and I kept thinking I was reading a Rosamunde Pilcher novel instead. Not that there's anything wrong with RP, I just missed the charm of Maeve Binchy's later books.<br /><br />The thing I love about Maeve Binchy's books is that they're generally speaking comfort reads. There are exceptions of course, but as a rule people tend to be in a better place at the end of the book than they were at the beginning. That is <i>not</i> the case with this book, and that - more than anything else - made me give it just 2 stars. It's the account of ~20 years of Elizabeth and Aisling's lives, and offers no resolution or has no real end... in fact, I was pretty shocked to see it end where it did. There seemed no rhyme or reason for it. It was as if Maeve Binchy suddenly realized how many pages she'd written already, and couldn't find a proper way to end it, so she just did.<br /><br />It had its moments, but as a whole I wasn't terribly impressed by it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8471955373785516931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1743291441" />
    <a title="Linda Fagioli-Katsiotas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25142878-linda-fagioli-katsiotas"><img alt="Linda Fagioli-Katsiotas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483041240p2/25142878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1743291441?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda Fagioli-Katsiotas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda Fagioli-Katsiotas" href="/user/show/25142878-linda-fagioli-katsiotas">Linda Fagioli-Katsiotas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1743291441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11912596062825178796">The author, Maeve Binchy, is my new most wonderful discovery. Unfortunately she is deceased, but fortunately she wrote some 15 books in her lifetime. Light a Penny Candle is a saga of two women who meet as children during WWII when 10-year-old Elizabeth is evacuated from London to live in safety with an Irish family, thereby meeting Aisling who becomes a life long friend. The author takes us through affairs, marriages and births of children and the characters are so real and endearing, I was dep</span>
  <span id="freeText11912596062825178796" style="display:none">The author, Maeve Binchy, is my new most wonderful discovery. Unfortunately she is deceased, but fortunately she wrote some 15 books in her lifetime. Light a Penny Candle is a saga of two women who meet as children during WWII when 10-year-old Elizabeth is evacuated from London to live in safety with an Irish family, thereby meeting Aisling who becomes a life long friend. The author takes us through affairs, marriages and births of children and the characters are so real and endearing, I was depressed to have lost them when the book ended. Binchy’s style is so artful with subtle lines here and there that bring surprising realizations to the reader. She weaves seemingly insignificant moments into the tale, which turn out to be integral to understanding the characters and the believability of their actions. I really like this story and I had to force myself not to go and buy all of Binchy’s books because there will be no new ones in the future, and although a Binchy-binge would be quite delicious, I want to savor her for a long time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11912596062825178796" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14745357354330489978">"'Mam, I'm far too old now to be sending silly cards with flowers and horseshoes on them to some woman in England that I can hardly remember.'<br/><br/>'Elizabeth White was reared in this house with you for five years like a sister, and you'll remember her as long as I say so,' said Eileen sharply."<br/><br/>Elizabeth White is sent from London, England, to live with her mother's school friend in Ireland during the Blitz.   <span id="freeText14745357354330489978" style="display:none">"'Mam, I'm far too old now to be sending silly cards with flowers and horseshoes on them to some woman in England that I can hardly remember.'<br /><br />'Elizabeth White was reared in this house with you for five years like a sister, and you'll remember her as long as I say so,' said Eileen sharply."<br /><br />Elizabeth White is sent from London, England, to live with her mother's school friend in Ireland during the Blitz. Elizabeth blossoms with her foster family and becomes especially close with the mother, Eileen, and one of the daughter's, the fiery Aisling O'Connor. Although they have very different personalities, Aisling and Elizabeth become lifelong best friends who will do anything for each other. As I tell my boyz, life is all about the choices you make -- the good, the bad, and everything in between.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139004398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18339176663432351836">O! Maeve Binchy...Ireland's own Jodi Picoult!<br/>If you prefer to not think too hard while reading; if you are amused by all things Irish; or if you've never experienced the Binchy formula, then you would probably enjoy any number of her books. Binchy, like Picoult, is best enjoyed in isolation of any of her other writings. <br/><br/>I believe this is one of her better books, but I am probably influenced by the fact that it was the first of hers that I read. It chronicles a couple of decades of friendship bet</span>
  <span id="freeText18339176663432351836" style="display:none">O! Maeve Binchy...Ireland's own Jodi Picoult!<br />If you prefer to not think too hard while reading; if you are amused by all things Irish; or if you've never experienced the Binchy formula, then you would probably enjoy any number of her books. Binchy, like Picoult, is best enjoyed in isolation of any of her other writings. <br /><br />I believe this is one of her better books, but I am probably influenced by the fact that it was the first of hers that I read. It chronicles a couple of decades of friendship between an Irish woman and an English woman through the trials and tribulations of their lives. Nothing revolutionary there, and yet it is quite charming for the better part of the book. Or so I thought when I first read it eleven years ago anyway. <br /><br /></span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344912889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8851847707446589883">When my mother handed me this book, I scoffed. I didn't read books like this -- it looked like some kind of wifty romance to me. But I was getting on a plane, so, okay, I took it. Started reading it as the plane took off from LAX -- and then, suddenly, we were landing at JFK and I had no idea where the time had gone. <br/><br/>Thus began my love affair with Maeve Binchy.<br/><br/>This book is the story of British Elizabeth and Irish Aisling, who meet when Elizabeth is sent to live in Ireland during the London Blitz</span>
  <span id="freeText8851847707446589883" style="display:none">When my mother handed me this book, I scoffed. I didn't read books like this -- it looked like some kind of wifty romance to me. But I was getting on a plane, so, okay, I took it. Started reading it as the plane took off from LAX -- and then, suddenly, we were landing at JFK and I had no idea where the time had gone. <br /><br />Thus began my love affair with Maeve Binchy.<br /><br />This book is the story of British Elizabeth and Irish Aisling, who meet when Elizabeth is sent to live in Ireland during the London Blitz. The rest of the story is their friendship, their families, and their lives, and it's so beautifully written and absolutely real that you actually miss the characters when you close the book.<br /><br />A lovely book, a lovely writer.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4501999379497451060">I first read this book almost 20 years ago - and loved it then as a teenager. So when I saw a copy in a second hand bookshop for $1 I had to buy it. Often when you return to an old favourite they have somehow shrunk with time but not this. MB is like putting on a comfortable cardie on a cold day and reminds me of hours spent reading in an armchair in our house which was tucked away out of site and where I could lose myself in a book for hours on end. This was one of her first and although her bo</span>
  <span id="freeText4501999379497451060" style="display:none">I first read this book almost 20 years ago - and loved it then as a teenager. So when I saw a copy in a second hand bookshop for $1 I had to buy it. Often when you return to an old favourite they have somehow shrunk with time but not this. MB is like putting on a comfortable cardie on a cold day and reminds me of hours spent reading in an armchair in our house which was tucked away out of site and where I could lose myself in a book for hours on end. This was one of her first and although her books are often derided for being too formulaic - there are times when you need not to think too hard and enjoy the story. For that reason alone she deserves a place in your library as a treasured and reliable friend.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0y3ENOR0RxAOTkNlVuzSqR/JIkotfYtpUuh3Z8+81H9s7P0ZBJ7ZbFdohmVO4PCBLklrXvRrc6NuLlXRXP/vdA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/YsKEeYfclsfGSckUsQbloW8tcY6C7R9Jn9pglQDinRCSjM8BvXsJ0Y/4iRKyDm+tDz80uMdTLcauUs0x0Cxfw==')})
  }

A Dublin landmark since its glory days the 1920s, Finbar\'s Hotel has grown increasingly shabby with the years. Now, on a night shortly before the grand old hotel is to be demolished, its rooms and corridors echo one last time with the voices of a curious collection of guests. On his first stay in a hotel, the middle-aged occupant of room 101 ponders the mysteries of the minibar and room service before charging out on the town in search of alcohol and adventure. Across the hall in 102, estranged sisters Ivy and Rose warily negotiate a long-avoided détente. A scorned lover turned catnapping desperado attempts to conceal his furry abductee in the wardrobe of room 103, while in room 107, a somewhat more accomplished thief goes stir-crazy plotting his escape with a small fortune in stolen paintings. Though none of the stories of iFinbar\'s Hotel/i are expressly attributed, close readings of these self-contained yet cleverly interconnected stories will undoubtedly lead to much speculation about       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3532.Maeve_Binchy">About Maeve Binchy</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3532.Maeve_Binchy"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1206566579p3/3532.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16909616407314014998">Maeve Binchy was born on 28 May 1940 in Dalkey, County Dublin, Ireland, the eldest child of four. Her parents were very positive and provided her with a happy childhood. Although she described herself as an overweight child, her parents' attitude gave her the confidence to accept herself for who she was.<br/><br/>She studied at University College Dublin and was a teacher for a while. She also loved travelin</span>
  <span id="freeText16909616407314014998" style="display:none">Maeve Binchy was born on 28 May 1940 in Dalkey, County Dublin, Ireland, the eldest child of four. Her parents were very positive and provided her with a happy childhood. Although she described herself as an overweight child, her parents' attitude gave her the confidence to accept herself for who she was.<br /><br />She studied at University College Dublin and was a teacher for a while. She also loved traveling, and this was how she found her niche as a writer. She liked going to different places, such as a Kibbutz in Israel, and she worked in a camp in the United States. While she was away, she sent letters home to her parents. They were so impressed with these chatty letters from all over the world that they decided to send them to a newspaper. After these letters were published, Maeve left teaching and became a journalist. <br /><br />Maeve married <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/175193._Gordon_Snell" title=" Gordon Snell" rel="nofollow noopener"> Gordon Snell</a>, writer and editor of children's books. When they were struggling financially, <i>Light a Penny Candle</i> was published, which made her an overnight success. Many of her books, such as <i>Echoes</i>, are set in the past in Ireland. Some of her later novels, such as <i>Evening Class</i>, take place in more modern times. Her books often deal with people who are young, fall in love, have families, and deal with relationship or family problems. The main characters are people whom readers can empathise with. <br /><br />She passed away on 30 July 2012, at the age of 72.<br /><br />Her cousin <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/249472._Dan_Binchy" title=" Dan Binchy" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dan Binchy</a> is also a published writer, as is her nephew <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/380602._Chris_Binchy" title=" Chris Binchy" rel="nofollow noopener"> Chris Binchy</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16909616407314014998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
